Saturday, 11:45 a.m. – Close to Home
------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

The largest Grand Prix in North American history doesn't happen without players from all over the place making their way to the Windy City. But Grand Prixs in the Midwest are a treat for the trove of Wisconsin players that have made a name for themselves. Adrian Sullivan, Brian Kowal, and Owen Turtenwald are among the throngs of locals vying for the title this weekend, and each one has a unique take on the format.


**Adrian Sullivan**  ![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Adrian-Sullivan.jpg)  

Mad deck-builder and Starcity Games columnist Adrian Sullivan is known for going a little rogue (and flipping a giant penny), and when he wasn't able to test as thoroughly for Legacy as he liked, he turned to a reliable source for deck-tech: Adrian Sullivan. Sporting an updated version of one of his past creations, Sullivan once again went outside even the metagame he envisions. "There will be lots of [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) decks, with [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) or [Dread](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dread)naughts, Goblins, some Storm, and after that the kitchen sink." Sullivan expects [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) variants to make up nearly half the top eight, with some number of Storm, Dredge, and Goblin lists rounding it out, plus "one surprise." Could that surprise be another Sullivan brew?


**Brian Kowal**  ![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Brian-Kowal.jpg)  

Brian Kowal is running pretty hot these days on the heels of a 22nd place finish in Kyoto and the resounding success of the R/W "Boat Brew" deck he's credited with creating. Like a number of other pros, Kowal hasn't tested nearly as much as he'd like. Also like a lot of pros, he's viewing Legacy through the lens of a certain [Coldsnap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coldsnap) enchantment. "This is going to be the [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) GP," said Kowal. "You have to have an answer to [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)."


For that reason, Kowal thinks Goblins should do unexpectedly well. "I probably should have played it myself, as good as it is," he said. "I mean, it's Goblins."


**Owen Turtenwald**  ![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Turtenwald.jpg)  

One player who knows exactly how good Goblins can be is Own Turtenwald, who took 2nd at Grand Prix Columbus running the little green men in a field full of Hulk Flash. Now, in a slightly less degenerate field, Owen thinks the tribe that would not die can do it again. "Goblins is better than people give it credit for," said Turtenwald. "And the [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) deck is overrated." Still, he thinks sheer numbers and the fact that [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) is the choice of many top pros will carry it to a few top eight appearance, alongside Goblins, Storm, and the pet of dealers everywhere, [Natural Order](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Natural+Order). Turtenwald had one more prediction, too: "The sky is blue, and LSV will win."

Saturday, 12:45 p.m. – Traveling from Afar
------------------------------------------


*by Bill Stark*

Blake covered some of the local heroes looking to make good on this Legacy weekend, but that's only one side of the story. Looking to steal the thunder out from underneath them are a host of the Pro Tour's biggest names, traveling from all over the world. We sat down to chat with a few of them regarding their thoughts on the format, predictions on the weekend, and more.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Juza.jpg)*Can playskill alone carry Martin Juza this weekend?*
Martin Juza has been on a tear over the past few months of the Pro Tour season, finishing as high as the Top 8 at Pro Tour-Berlin. He came into this weekend hoping for a solid finish, but had a sheepish admission when questioned about how much preparation he had managed to get in. "Zero testing." He responded, adding "I looked at some decks online and compiled a deck from that." What did he think the best deck in the format is? "Dredge. Maybe Goblins if players don't have the hate for it." And his prediction on most played deck? "[Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)/Top."


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/LSV.jpg)*Luis mugs for the camera with fellow Kyoto finalist Gabriel Nassif*
Second on the list was Luis Scott-Vargas, a player famous enough to need no introduction. He's fresh off his Pro Tour finals appearance just a weekend ago in Kyoto, where he was playing Black-White Tokens. How much prep had he gotten in? "I like Legacy, but not as much [testing] as I would have liked." He had the same answer for both which deck was the best in the format and which deck would be the most popular: "[Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)/Top." He was quick to lean in, adding "A lot of people will be playing [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus), but I think it's not that good. We may find out that it's really cool, but not the right call."


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Bucher.jpg)*Manuel Bucher spends more time in America than Europe these days!*
Finally we have Manuel Bucher, who has practically become adopted by a group of Michigan players and spent more time on the North American continent in 2009 than on his native European one. "I've been playing Legacy since getting back from Kyoto," he explained when asked about how much testing he had done for the event. He also parroted LSV in naming [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)/Top as both the most powerful deck in Legacy as well as the most played this weekend. His prediction for the winning deck, however? "I predict Faeries will win!"


  


Round 2: Richard Feldman vs. Sean Weihe
---------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

Richard Feldman, longtime Starcity Games writer, came out pretty boldly and pretty publicly earlier this week that Dredge was The Deck to Play. He backed it up by bringing the graveyard-flooding monstrosity to the table in Chicago.


Sean Weihe is a regional player from Mankato, Minn. who claims he played Legacy “before [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)” (hereafter known as B.Cb.), but not much since (A.Cb.). But he was running Merfolk, a decidedly new-flavored deck from the A.Cb. Era that harkens back to Fish while running new standouts from Lorwyn like [Silvergill Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silvergill+Adept), [Cursecatcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cursecatcher), and [Merrow Reejerey](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Merrow+Reejerey).


Neither player had dice or any sort of randomization device, so instead of a roll-off, Sean won the odd “coverage reporter writes down an even or odd number and the players guess which it is.” For the record it was 456. I have no idea why.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Sean-Weihe.jpg)**Game 1**  

Sean kept his opener while Richard sent his back for a better six. Dredge is known for being able to mulligan well, so successively lower hands weren't necessarily a problem. Sean led with [Flooded Strand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flooded+Strand) into an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) of the basic variety before playing an [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial). Richard countered with a blind [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) naming [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). He hit (you sunk my battleship!) one and revealed a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland), [Standstill](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Standstill), [Silvergill Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silvergill+Adept) and [Merrow Reejerey](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Merrow+Reejerey).


Sean ran the turn 2 [Standstill](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Standstill) out, banking on his [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial) to get him there. Richard wasted no time in breaking with a [Tireless Tribe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tireless+Tribe). Sean vialed out a [Cursecatcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cursecatcher) then played a Silvergill adept on his turn before he passed back.


Richard had no upkeep discard, instead choosing to draw a card and play a [Gemstone Mine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gemstone+Mine). Instead he discarded [Golgari Thug](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Thug) and cast [Breakthrough](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Breakthrough) for one, netting a Narcomeba in the process, but not finding any more dredgers to rev his engine.


But the engine was almost immediately stuck in neutral, as the cagey Minnesotan revealed his maindeck surprise, [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus).


“Maindeck?!”  

“Yeah, why not,” reasoned Sean.  

“Wow. Bold.”


After that, Richard could only laugh and pass back.


“I'm going to keep my composure, I did see that coming,” Richard offered before swinging in with a lonely Narcomeba.


Sean added a [Mutavault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mutavault) to the table and [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Aether%2BVial)ed out a Merrow Reejery during combat, followed up with a [Wake Thrasher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wake+Thrasher), who was a very angry 8/8 after Richard passed with no play.


When Sean [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Aether%2BVial)ed out a second Reejery and played a [Cursecatcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cursecatcher) to tap both blockers, Richard was forced to scoop up the very important Game 1.


Sean Weihe 1 Richard Feldman 0


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Richard-Feldman.jpg)**Game 2**  

Between games they debated the relative merits of the main-deck [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus), as much of Dredge's game plan revolves around winning a hate-free Game 1. Maindeck Relic changes that equation quite handedly.


Richard led with a turn one [Pithing Needle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pithing+Needle) on [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus), while Sean could only pass with a [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta).


Richard then cast [Careful Study](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Careful+Study), pitching [Golgari Grave-Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Grave-Troll) and [Bridge from Below](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bridge+from+Below), then played a 2nd Study to dredge, hitting mostly blanks. He discarded two dredgers and passed.


Sean's second turn only made a [Silvergill Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silvergill+Adept) while revealing a [Cursecatcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cursecatcher).


Richard then lined up a pretty monster turn three, as dredge does so often. Richard dredged then cast [Breakthrough](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Breakthrough) for zero, milling most of his library in the process and netting two [Narcomoeba](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Narcomoeba)s. He then popped [Cephalid Coliseum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cephalid+Coliseum) to kill nearly the rest of his library. Four [Narcomoeba](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Narcomoeba)s started sacrificing themselves for the greater good, one for [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) naming [Tormod's Crypt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tormod%27s+Crypt). Sean revealed two [Echoing Truth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Echoing+Truth)s, [Standstill](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Standstill), a [Cursecatcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cursecatcher), and another Adept. When all was said and done, Richard had accumulated eight zombies, two [Narcomoeba](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Narcomoeba)s and a 22/22 Grave Troll.


“Geeze, I feel done. Go.”


Sean ran out a [Cursecatcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cursecatcher) as a blocker, and passed back.


Richard triggered three [Ichorid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ichorid)s on his upkeep, then swung in with the team. The zombie tokens were hit by [Echoing Truth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Echoing+Truth), and the three [Ichorid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ichorid)s took Sean down to 10. The attack did, however, cost Richard his [Bridge from Below](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bridge+from+Below)s.


Sean didn't find the right answer this time, and three [Ichorid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ichorid)s got there on Richard's next turn.


Sean Weihe 1 Richard Feldman 1


**Game 3**  

Sean, on the play, kept his seven, as did Richard. Sean went to 19 to fetch out a basic [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island), and led with [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial). Richard countered with his own one mana enabler in [Tireless Tribe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tireless+Tribe).


Sean simply played a [Mutavault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mutavault) and passed with no action. Richard discarded a [Darkblast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Darkblast) and started dredging on turn two thanks to two Careful Studies. Sean simply vialed in a [Cursecatcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cursecatcher) at end of turn, then ran out a [Wake Thrasher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wake+Thrasher) on his own turn, threatening a large attacker.


Richard started turn three by bringing out an [Ichorid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ichorid), and followed with a draw step dredge and a [Cephalid Coliseum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cephalid+Coliseum) sacrifice, jumping three [Narcomoeba](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Narcomoeba)s into play along the way. Richard attempted to flash back a [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy), but [Cursecatcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cursecatcher) countered the offending discard spell and removed the balance of the [Bridge from Below](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bridge+from+Below)s in Richard's graveyard.


Sean simply attacked with a 5/5 [Wake Thrasher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wake+Thrasher) on his next turn, which was blocked effectively by a [Tireless Tribe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tireless+Tribe), then added a Merrow Reejery before passing back. Richard re-grew three [Ichorid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ichorid)s and swung in with all of them and three [Narcomoeba](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Narcomoeba)s before his attempted [Dread Return](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dread+Return) was countered by [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will).


Sean simply untapped and attacked with two Merfolk, and again Richard had two discards to block the [Wake Thrasher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wake+Thrasher). On his upkeep, Richard brought back the full playset of [Ichorid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ichorid)s as his library ticked town toward empty. He then attacked with all four [Ichorid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ichorid)s and two [Narcomoeba](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Narcomoeba)s. The [Ichorid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ichorid)s were [Echoing Truth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Echoing+Truth)ed, leaving Sean holding on at four life after the attack.


Still, Sean sorted through his cards trying to get eight points past Richard's [Tireless Tribe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tireless+Tribe) and single untapped [Narcomoeba](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Narcomoeba). The [Wake Thrasher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wake+Thrasher) itself was big enough at 8/8 to do the damage on its own, but Sean wasn't sure he could get around Richard's “Tireless” defenses. In the end, he swung with only two men, and clocked Richard down to six before playing [Cursecatcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cursecatcher) to untap his [Wake Thrasher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wake+Thrasher) with Reejerey's ability.


It wasn't enough, as though only three [Ichorid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ichorid)s could return this time around, three was enough to do the job as Richard swung for exactly lethal with a single card left in his library.


Richard Feldman defeats Sean Weihe 2-1


  


Round 3: Carlos Irizarry vs. Patrick Chapin
-------------------------------------------


*by Bill Stark*

Patrick Chapin is a many of many **Magic** hats, writer, deck designer, famous pro, VIP. He entered the third round of Grand Prix-Chicago short a bye that would have guaranteed him a 3-0 start on the weekend. His opponent for the round, Carlos Irizarry, was less well known but didn't flinch, winning the die roll and opening on a [Tropical Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tropical+Island). Chapin played an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) of his own, albeit of the basic variety, then a [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Rd3_Irizarry.jpg)*Carlos Irizarry makes his debut in the Feature Match area.*Irizarry, facing a tapped out opponent, was all too happy to stick a [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance), and the match was shaping up to be a drawn out, control on control bloodbath. When Chapin attempted to play a [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) of his own a turn later, Carlos responded with [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm). He reset the top three cards of his deck, then attempted to reveal for his [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance). That prompted a judge call from Pat.


“If [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) is a may trigger, does my opponent have to declare it going on the stack before he [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)s?” The judge ruled in Pat's favor, meaning Irizarry couldn't reveal from his [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance). However, Irizarry had a [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) hardcast to counter the troublesome enchantment anyway, and Chapin was forced to pass the turn without making a land drop. Looking to capitalize, Irizarry played [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator), then [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) a turn later, completing his [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) lock.


Chapin took a final peek at the top three cards of his deck then, seeing no help coming soon, opted to concede from a very bad board position. The drawn out control mirror hadn't panned out at all, and the players reached for their sideboard with forty minutes on the clock.


Irizarry 1,


[Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) was the first play of the second game, and it came from Patrick Chapin when Carlos Irizarry attempted a first-turn [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top). The *Alliances* powerhouse was enough to prevent the artifact from hitting play, but a turn later Carlos was able to resolve [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) unmolested from Chapin.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Rd3_Chapin.jpg)*Could Patrick Chapin overcome a rough Game 1?*Unlike the first game, Patrick Chapin was finding himself plenty of lands, but after his opponent's [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) had resolved, Pat fell increasingly behind on the board. In addition to his *Coldsnap* enchantment, Carlos had managed to add both [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top)*and* [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) to his board. The game wasn't looking good for Chapin, and he was forced to do something about it.


At 12 life, Pat played [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) targeting the ‘Goyf. Carlos activated his Divining Top in response, the moved to reveal for [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance). Chapin pointed at the enchantment saying “You forgot to trigger it again,” and Carlos rolled his eyes in frustration. Clearly his longtime pro opponent wasn't going to give him any inches in the matchup.


Irizarry found himself a second [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), but Chapin was ready. He used [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip) to blow up [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance), then used a second [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) to hit the [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). When Carlos tried a second copy of [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance), Chapin was ready with [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), but he didn't have an immediate answer for a 1/1 [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) Irizarry played in the same turn.


Both players were missing land drops, with Carlos Irizarry stuck on three while Chapin had four. Trying to get ahead in the card count, Pat played and successfully resolved [Intuition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intuition), hunting up [Life from the Loam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Life+from+the+Loam), [Windswept Heath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Windswept+Heath), and [Lonely Sandbar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lonely+Sandbar). Carlos gave him the [Windswept Heath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Windswept+Heath), then spent his own turn playing a third copy of [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). Chapin didn't seem fazed, cracking his [Windswept Heath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Windswept+Heath) to find [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor), then tapping four mana to play [Natural Order](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Natural+Order). It was a techy series of plays that potentially could end with Chapin having [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus) in play. Irizarry spun his [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top), desperately hoping for an answer, and looked to the heavens thankfully when he found one: [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to counter [Natural Order](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Natural+Order). Chapin nodded, and passed the turn.


Carlos quickly sent his team in to the red zone, attacking Chapin down to just 2 life. He played a post-combat [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) before shipping the turn, but the play may have been a mistake. With six cards in his graveyard, just one card short of threshold, Carlos could have attempted to find a means of getting a single spell into his graveyard pre-combat against a tapped out Chapin, then attacked for exactly lethal as his Mongoose got +2/+2. It was moot in any case as Chapin was unable to stick an answer on his own turn, and Irizarry attacked for lethal, ending the match in his favor.


Carlos Irizarry 2, Patrick Chapin 0


*Editor's Note: After the match, the ruling regarding Counterbalance was brought to the attention of head judge Jason Ness. He issued a corrected version of the ruling that will allow players to trigger their Counterbalance even if they've used abilities or played cards in response to a spell without specifically pointing out that they're leaving a Counterbalance trigger on the stack.*


  


Saturday, 2:20 p.m. – Steve Sadin, Legacy King
----------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

It's been a few years since Steve Sadin rocked Columbus with Hulk Flash, but that doesn't mean the reigning Legacy king has lifted his finger from the pulse of the format. That pulse, though, hasn't really changed much, he said.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Steve-Sadin.jpg)Not much out of Shards or Conflux particularly excited him, though he acknowledged the much ballyhooed existence of [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus). Other than that, he doesn't see that much has changed since the Legacy portion of Worlds. So much so, that he based his deck choice off that very assumption.


“There is [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus), but it's not something I'd play,” said Sadin. “It's just a creature. I don't want to invest four slots on a kill unless it's really fast. If I get into an attrition war, I don't want to start drawing blanks.”


Beyond the decks headlined by Legacy's version of [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker) for [Darksteel Colossus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Darksteel+Colossus), Sadin sees a wide-open field full of “a lot of [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) decks, and 8-10 other decks. Like Affinity, Dredge, Survival, Stax, and Goblins.”


He nodded toward 42-land and combo as well, but said he expected “[Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) decks are going to do extremely well. And I wouldn't be surprised if Dredge puts a few in the Top 8, as a lot of people completely removed their Dredge hate from their sideboards.”


It's a far cry from Columbus' “Flash or no?” metagame that Sadin sat atop, but the crown is his until Sunday at least. Until then, someone will have to take it from him.


  


Saturday, 2:43 p.m. – Poor Nate Price
-------------------------------------


*by Bill Stark*

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Price.jpg)Being a coverage writer is hard, sometimes thankless work, but to keep fresh many reporters relish the chance to cut their teeth at premier events like Grand Prixs. Nate Price, fresh off the coverage team from Pro Tour-Kyoto, found himself in those shoes this weekend as he set forth to battle using the Legacy format. After just one round, he looked a bit bruised and battered.


“How come no one told me there was second-turn [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus) in this format?” The Indianapolis native questioned, exasperatedly. Inquiring further into what he meant, he explained “My opponent, Brian Gustafson, opened on first turn Gaea's Cradle, remove Elvish Spirit Guide to play [Llanowar Elves](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Llanowar+Elves), play a second Elf with Cradle, go, untap, [Natural Order](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Natural+Order) for [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus).” A rough beat to be certain, particularly when you consider the fact Nate himself had simply opened on [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) and [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top). As they say, welcome to Legacy!


  


Round 4 Gabriel Nassif vs. Charles Gindy
----------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

With the three bye rounds out of the way, the pros have flooded into the standings. And while many pros are still playing against the Joes, the round four feature match pits two pro tour champions against one another.


Two pro tour champions, the imitable Gabriel Nassif only one week removed from winning Pro Tour Kyoto, and Charles Gindy who also won a Standard Pro Tour when he took PT Hollywood in 2008 with B/G Elves.


Both past champions were sporting pretty similar looks at the Countertop archetype, with Gindy opting for a few more animals with [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose).


**Game 1**  

Both players kept their initial hands, and Gindy led with [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta) into [Underground Sea](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Underground+Sea) into [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder). Nassif skipped the Delta and just ran [Underground Sea](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Underground+Sea) into [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top), signaling the mirror.


Gindy had the turn two [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant), which Nassif allowed after considerable, um, consideration.


“This is going to be a boring game,” offered Gindy as Nassif Topped on his upkeep.  

“Yes,” Nassif offered, content to just play [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta) and pass.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Charles-Gindy.jpg)Gindy continued to lay pressure on the board with a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) after some Bob beats put Nassif to 18. Nassif again thought long and hard before declining to respond to Gindy's second brutal two-drop.


Nassif countered with his own important two-drop with [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance), which Gindy allowed to resolve. Resolving [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)/Top was key to controlling the match-up between these similar decks.


Gindy's Confidant revealed another, and Gindy tried to then cast his own [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance), which Nassif allowed to resolve despite activating [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) in response. Gindy, aware the air was clear for more spells that cost two, dropped yet another [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant), and then dropped Nassif to 12 on the attack.


The Kyoto champ's response to Gindy's growing horde was [Vedalken Shackles](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vedalken+Shackles), a card that could turn the game around if given enough time. An upkeep-revealed Mongoose could get around Shackles, but only if it could first get around [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance).


Gindy attempted a pre-combat [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), which Nassif stopped with [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance). When Gindy attempted his own Top, Nassif was ready by flipping his with [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) on the stack. Gindy attacked Nassif to three, then played his third [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) of the match, threatening lethal even if [Vedalken Shackles](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vedalken+Shackles) did its thing.


[Sower of Temptation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sower+of+Temptation) was another story altogether. Gindy declined to reveal for [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) in response to the four-cost faerie, and saw [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) and [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) on his upkeep from his dual [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant)s. Unfortunately, Nassif had the Swords on top of his deck to counter the game-winning spell.


“I hope your hand is only ones,” said Nassif.


It was good enough, as Gindy simply passed back without attacking, possibly hoping to kill Nassif, who was now at 3, with [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant). Indeed, Nassif dropped to two on his upkeep when he revealed the known [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares).


When Nassif tried to resolve Sensei's Divining top the next turn, a flurry of instants and [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)s from both players - two from Gindy and one from Nassif - ended with Nassif forced to reveal a blind [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance). He revealed...[Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder).


“That was all for nothing,” laughed Nassif as he eventually resolved [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) and then Shacklesed the [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). Upkeep reveals on [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) took Gindy to five and left him with a full grip, but with no plays for his turn he passed back, with Nassif at one and needing to reveal a land to his [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant).


“No land in the top three,” Gindy pleaded. And, indeed, Nassif had no land in the top three, which forced him to [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) the stolen [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) with Bob on the stack. He had a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) of his own to follow up, but a blind [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) held the fort for the moment. Nassif then ended his turn by attacking with the [Sower of Temptation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sower+of+Temptation) to drop Gindy to three, and a [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder)-induced shuffle.


On his upkeep, Gindy's two Confidants revealed a [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) and...[Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will).


Gabriel Nassif 1 Charles Gindy 0


During the break they both lamented the ponderous nature of the mirror. Top, [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance), [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant), and...


“We took half an hour,” pointed out Nassif.  

“Geeze,” said Gindy.  

“We'll try and play a little faster.”  

“Faster than the last one at least.”


**Game 2**  

Both kept and Gindy led with a turn one “good in the mirror” [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) while Nassif had [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island), [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top). Just how good in the mirror the Mongoose that could was would be evident shortly (foreshadowing!)


[Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) from Gindy met [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) from Nassif, and he followed up with a [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) of his own. [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) failed to find a way through [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance), and Gindy was resolved to simply swing.


On his turn, Nassif cast two Tops, then passed while tapped out, inducing Gindy to play a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant). Nassif had the two-drop on the top of his deck, and the subsequent Top flip to stop another Mongoose, especially important now that Gindy had Threshold.


[Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) began to put Nassif ahead in every metric except life total, and his turn consisted of multiple Top activations and [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)s, while [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) attacked back at Gindy.


On his turn, Gindy continued to attack, putting Nassif to six with his single Mongoose. Able to freely counter anything his opponent plays, Nassif seemed unbothered by the 3/3 shroud. That would change.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Nimble-Mongoose.jpg)More Top activations, more fetch lands, and another Top rounded out Nassifs turn, while Gindy was content to simply attack and pass. Nassif blocked with his Confidant to preserve his life total while at six, then searched for an answer to Gindy's Mongoose during his main phase with another flurry of Top activations and [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)s. He finally played a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) to chump block, and passed, while Gindy played “attack go” once again.


The following turn he found the answer he was looking for in [Perish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Perish). Gindy, however, had the right answer in [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) and, despite having the “lock,” Nassif was forced to scoop his cards even though Gindy resolved approximately one spell all game. That one spell was a doozy, though.


Charles Gindy 1 Gabriel Nassif 1


**Game 3**  

After an epic Game 1 and a significantly faster paced Game 2, under seven minutes remained for the penultimate game. Both players kept, noticeably playing faster than previous games.


Nassif led with fetch land into [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), and Gindy followed suit with fetch land into [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top), though Nassif had the [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze).


Nassif's own Top hit, and Gindy tried to resolve [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance). Nassif's second [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) once again held Gindy back.


Gindy struck back by [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip)ping Nassif's Top, but Nassif simply untapped and offered a replacement. Naturally, Gindy had the second [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip).


And since he's Gabriel Nassif, he calmly untapped and played his third [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top).


“Must be,” said Gindy.


Gindy then resolved his own Top and a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), and Nassif had a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) end of turn to set up a Countrbalance on his own turn. Nassif had the controlling combo again, but was once again facing a fat green creature on the board, albeit one he could actually target.


The [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) took Nassif to 14, and Gindy tried a second, which resolved. Sower, however, took it right away.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Gabriel-Nassif.jpg)Gindy then resolved a [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) on his own turn to level the playing field. Nassif's [Threads of Disloyalty](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Threads+of+Disloyalty) was out of [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) reach, however, and stole [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). Nassif swung for seven and passed with lethal on the board. When Gindy couldn't resolve a [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) the following turn, he offered his hand to last week's Pro Tour champ.


Gabriel Nassif defeats Charles Gindy 2-1


  


Saturday, 4:45 p.m. - Shards in Legacy
--------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

While everyone is always excited to break out their dual lands, [Goblin Lackey](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Lackey)s, [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)s, and [Hecatomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hecatomb)s (I saw it, I swear), a number of new cards from Shards of Alara and Conflux have made their way all the way to Legacy.



![Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=PROGENITUS)

The talk of the weekend was, of course, [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus) (via [Natural Order](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Natural+Order)), and as of round five the 10/10 had several players lurking hear the top tables. Pregenitus decks came in several variations, as some players tacked it (alongside [Werebear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Werebear) and [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor)) onto Threshold/[Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) decks. Others (like [Nate Price's round one opponent](http://www.wizards.com/magic/magazine/article.aspx?x=mtg/daily/eventcoverage/gpchi09/welcome#7)) tried to run out the monster turn two through various elves and fast mana, often combined with a [Survival of the Fittest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Survival+of+the+Fittest) engine.


[Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus), however, has been the biggest news, and probably the most played, Shards or Conflux card on the weekend. Relic has been a replacement or a supplement to [Tormod's Crypt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tormod%27s+Crypt) and other graveyard-hating sideboard cards. Some even justify running it maindeck, since it cycles in a pinch.


[Ad Nauseam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ad+Nauseam) found its place in Legacy immediately upon its release in Storm-based decks, and many players have been seen paying five mana and nearly all their life to draw upwards of 20 cards. Finding enough cards to produce a lethal [Tendrils of Agony](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tendrils+of+Agony) after that is fairly academic.



![Elspeth, Knight-Errant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Elspeth%2C+Knight-Errant)

Prison-style decks have a smattering of showings here and there, helped out by a few Shards and Conflux beauties. [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) is an answer to, well, pretty much anything (except, of course, [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus)). Elspeth, [Knight Errant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+Errant) provides a tough-to-kill win condition, as well as food for [Smokestack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smokestack) and [Tangle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tangle)wire, and seems to be standard in White Prison lists. [Path to Exile](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Path+to+Exile) has seen play, but usually in its “four more Swords” role, as in  [Jaime Cano's Grand Prix Trial-winning deck](http://archive.wizards.com/%20http://www.wizards.com/magic/magazine/article.aspx?x=mtg/daily/eventcoverage/gpchi09/welcome#2). Another GPT-winning deck by Fredrick Chang played a single [Sigil of Distinction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sigil+of+Distinction) in his mono-blue Faerie-Stompy deck, a deck that runs cheap blue creatures with bonuses and supplements them with explosive equipment like [Sword of Light and Shadow](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Light+and+Shadow)


Other cards have helped supplement old strategies. [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary) is fairly common in combo and non-combo elf decks alike, and [Wild Nacatl](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wild+Nacatl) has seen play in both Zoo-ish decks and alongside [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) and friends as a more reliably large [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose). Other aggro decks have readily adopted [Tidehollow Sculler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tidehollow+Sculler) and [Hellspark Elemental](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellspark+Elemental) as well, both likely ports from Extended decks.


Finally, Conflux was spotted on the floor, but in a list of 68 cards. We're pretty sure it's not the hot new tech, but we applaud someone for trying.


  


Round 5 Feature Match: Luis Scott-Vargas vs. Carlos Romao
---------------------------------------------------------


*by Bill Stark*

“Do you have a die?” Carlos asked his opponent Luis as they sat down in the feature match area.


“No,” he responded, adding “do you?” When it became apparent neither of the two had a means of randomly determining who would begin the game, they turned to the crowd of onlookers for help.


“Do you guys need dice?” A bystander asked, offering up a six-sider. Luis managed to win the die roll, opening on the play and a [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta). The California standout is on an absolute tear over the past few months, with a Pro Tour win, Pro Tour finals appearance, Pro Tour Top 16, and two Grand Prix titles to his resume. Were it not for Gabriel Nassif's Pro Tour win over Luis in Kyoto just one week ago, there's no doubt he would have claimed the title of “best player on Tour” with no resistance.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/FM5_Romao.jpg)*Former World Champion Carlos Romao.*Be that as it may, Carlos Romao was certainly no slouch. The former World Champion spent his early turns cycling lands, playing [Mox Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mox+Diamond), and setting a [Chalice of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chalice+of+the+Void) on one, a solid start for his Aggro Loam deck. Luis Scott-Vargas played right through, dropping a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) on the second turn and a [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator) the turn after. The 2/3 *Dissension* uncommon gave Carlos pause, as he'd need to come up with an answer or the critter would munch his Mox and Chalice.


An answer he had, in the form of [Devastating Dreams](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devastating+Dreams) for three. Luis waited for his opponent to finish discarding three cards for the spell, then nodded, allowing it to resolve. The play left Romao with his Mox and Chalice on one, but he immediately began skipping land drops. Unfortunately for him, his opponent wasted no time getting back on the board, dropping a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) followed by back-to-back [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf)s. Thanks to the [Devastating Dreams](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devastating+Dreams), the Goyfs were gigantic, and LSV made a heads-up play to give them +1/+1 by dropping [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top). With Carlos' Chalice on one, the Top was countered and added a new card type to the graveyard. Romao nodded at the play, then conceded, too far behind to catch up and staring down too many giant monsters.


Luis Scott-Vargas 1, Carlos Romao 0


The second game kicked off with a very aggressive start from Carlos Romao, who played a sac-land to find [Taiga](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Taiga), a [Mox Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mox+Diamond) discarding [Volrath's Stronghold](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Volrath%27s+Stronghold), then used his two mana to play [Life from the Loam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Life+from+the+Loam) to get his lands right back. Luis Scott-Vargas wasn't impressed, opening on a first-turn [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus) which he immediately used to nail the [Life from the Loam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Life+from+the+Loam) and set his opponent's primary game plan back a step.


Romao didn't let on how painful the play was for him, instead re-playing his [Wooded Foothills](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wooded+Foothills) from the first turn, then a [Chalice of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chalice+of+the+Void) set to one. Scott-Vargas was happy to play [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance), then [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) a turn later, but the Brazilian was ready for the troublesome *Coldsnap* enchantment. He flipped [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip) onto the board, killing the enchantment after Luis failed to reveal a three-drop to counter from the top of his deck. The split second ability of [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip) meant Luis wasn't able to respond with activated abilities, but because [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)‘s effect is a triggered ability, he got one usage out of it to try to get lucky in countering the Grip. It was a bummer for him to miss, but the heads-up pro didn't let the [Disenchant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disenchant) sneak by without at least *attempting* to stop it.


[Countryside Crusher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Countryside+Crusher) soon joined the team of Carlos Romao, and grew into a 6/6. Luis answered by playing a second [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), but his board position wasn't that great as Carlos just fired right back with a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) of his own and a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant). Trying to gain some traction, Luis played [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator) but an attack from the Crusher put the totals at 16-12 in Carlos' favor.


The 2/3 Predator got through in the air, eating the [Chalice of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chalice+of+the+Void) set to one and allowing Luis to play two copies of [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) in one turn. Romao opted to use a second [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip) to blow up Scott-Vargas' [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus), then attacked with both his Crusher and [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). Luis quickly put both of his own ‘Goyfs in front of his opponent's, then used [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) to off the Crusher. Romao split the damage from his [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) amongst both of the American's, indicating a possible post-combat [Devastating Dreams](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devastating+Dreams).


Instead, Carlos used [Burning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burning+Wish) to find Morningtide after exiting the attack step. By removing both graveyards from the game, Carlos ensured the death of his opponent's [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf)s and ended the turn well ahead on land with [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) on the board and [Life from the Loam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Life+from+the+Loam) in his hand. Luis wasn't exactly out of things, however, as he dropped a [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) to join his [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top)s on the table and blew up Romao's [Mox Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mox+Diamond) by attacking with [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator). By the time Scott-Vargas passed the turn, it was 14-10 in his favor.


[Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip) hit the table for Carlos, who used the instant to blow up [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance). That freed him up to start getting back on the [Life from the Loam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Life+from+the+Loam) train, and he soon found himself a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) as well. Naturally Romao's ‘Goyf came a turn after the Pro Tour-Berlin champ had played one of his own, but the board was soon cleared entirely of creatures as Carlos used [Devastating Dreams](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devastating+Dreams) to [Armageddon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Armageddon) Luis and [Wrath of God](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Wrath%2Bof%2BGod) both of the players. With his opponent having access to [Life from the Loam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Life+from+the+Loam), four mana, and [Volrath's Stronghold](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Volrath%27s+Stronghold) to start recurring [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf)s, Luis Scott-Vargas conceded.


Luis Scott-Vargas 1, Carlos Romao 1


The opening turns of the third game were all about card drawing; Luis Scott-Vargas plopped [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) onto the board while Carlos Romao made [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant), accelerated thanks to an opening [Mox Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mox+Diamond). Luis played the second half of his “combo” on his second turn by dropping [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance), then snagged a free counter from it as he blindly revealed a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) on the top of his deck to counter Carlos Romao's attempt to [Burning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burning+Wish).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/FM5_LSV.jpg)*LSV's hot streak keep going?* Luis played the 2/1 when he was given the turn back, then passed with a [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta) up. The two pros had thirteen minutes left to finish their match, so both went on the warpath with their [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant)s. That left the totals 14-13 in Luis' favor, and he played [Tormod's Crypt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tormod%27s+Crypt) to threaten Romao's valuable resource: the graveyard. The Brazilian didn't seem overly concerned, attacking one of his opponent's valuable resources in lands by using back to back [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)s to keep Luis' mana flow tied up.


The two continued with attacks putting the totals at 10-8 in Luis' favor when Carlos attempted a [Seismic Assault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seismic+Assault). The American took a spin of his Top and used a sac-land to try to find a way to prevent the troublesome enchantment from resolving, but nothing was forthcoming and the [Seismic Assault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seismic+Assault) stuck. Carlos immediately pitched a land to blow up Luis' Confidant, then passed the turn.


[Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip) managed to find its way to the American's side of the table, and he used it to dispatch the [Seismic Assault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seismic+Assault), but he still needed to find a solution to the 2/1 Confidant beating him down. He did exactly that as he plucked a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) from the top of his deck and cast it. The tables had turned! Now it was up to Carlos to find a solution to the very large ‘Goyf, or risk taking lethal damage as his life total had fallen to just 5. He didn't find a removal spell, but at least he had a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) to block.


Or so he thought. Luis spun his Top again at the end of Carlos' turn, finding a [Sower of Temptation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sower+of+Temptation). The 2/2 allowed him to steal the chump blocker, paving the way for him to attack for lethal and the match.


Luis Scott-Vargas 2, Carlos Romao 1


  


Saturday, 6:25 p.m. - Photo Essay
---------------------------------


*by Bill Stark*

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/CedTop.jpg)*Cedric Phillips is all business on top…*![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/CedBottom.jpg)*…all party on bottom.*![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/LSVGerryT.jpg)*Luis Scott-Vargas and Gerry Thompson, an imposing site at any Grand Prix.*![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Ness.jpg)*Head Judge Jason Ness gives a shout out to his students at Bow Valley High School.*![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Style.jpg)*A player who knows how to ride in style.*![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Hochman.jpg)*Tournament Organizer Alan Hochman models the spiffy GP-Chicago playmat, free to players!*![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Alexander.jpg)*Special guest: artist Rob Alexander.*  


Round 6 Feature Match: AJ Sacher vs. Ari Lax
--------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

AJ Sacher and Ari Lax are up-and-coming players and writers who find themselves at 4-1 slightly past the midway point of the giant GP. Ari was fresh off a narrow miss in Kyoto, where he finished in 15th place, missing out on the Top 8 near the end. AJ Sacher meanwhile had placed as high at 19th at Berlin and has been chronicling his adventures for TCGplayer.com as of late.


Both players were slightly surprised to find themselves in a feature match.


“Are we serious the best people? Are we seriously the feature match?” wondered Ari. “I'm like 0-x in feature matches. And by 0-x I mean 0-2.”


Both players had a gift for the gab as they chatted about past formats at lightning speed while shuffling up, recalling long-gone metagame with ease.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Ari%20Lax.jpg)*Ari Lax* They brought radically different decks to Chicago, with AJ opting for the long-game potential of [Survival of the Fittest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Survival+of+the+Fittest), while Ari sleeved up Dredge.


**Game 1**  

AJ kept his six and led with [Dryad Arbor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Arbor).


“Yeah, I know what you're playing,” offered Ari, who ended his turn with no play in order to discard [Golgari Grave-Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Grave-Troll), signaling he was running the dredge engine.


AJ followed up with his own engine in a turn two [Survival of the Fittest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Survival+of+the+Fittest), while Ari merely dredged and played a [Tarnished Citadel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarnished+Citadel). The Citadel wasn't long for the word, however, as AJ sent it to the [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) the following turn, then discarded [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) to search up the quirky dredge-slaying Spore Fog and play it.


Ari dredged, played a Cephalid Colesium and again had to pass the turn with no action. AJ attacked and ran out [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), who was rather large thanks to the dredge action on the other side of the board. AJ merely drew and discarded before, once again, passing back.


A [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) from AJ named [Breakthrough](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Breakthrough), missed, but saw two [Bridge from Below](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bridge+from+Below), one [Narcomoeba](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Narcomoeba), a [Dread Return](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dread+Return) and three dredgers. AJ then used Survival to find [Squee, Goblin Nabob](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squee%2C+Goblin+Nabob) to jump start his engine. Flashback on Therapy hit [Golgari Thug](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Thug), before Ari once again played draw-go.


With his engine running on all cylinders, AJ found and played [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant), which revealed a damaging [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) the following turn. After dredging nothing of consequence, Ari scooped.


“I think I actually want to board in 15 cards,” said Ari. “That did not end well.”


AJ Sacher 1 Ari Lax 0


**Game 2**  

Again while shuffling up the two traded thoughts on the very match-up they were playing.


“How's your match-up here?” Ari asked. Whether he was fishing for information or just continuing to chatter is hard to say.  

“Eh, it's alright.”  

“Better when you win Game 1, I bet,” to which AJ obviously could nod in agreement.


Again AJ has to trade seven for six, while Ari keeps and leads with a [Gemstone Mine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gemstone+Mine) and nothing. AJ has the first turn [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial), while Ari kicks off the dredging with an end of turn [Firestorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Firestorm). However, the next turn dredge reveals nothing relevant and Ari passes the turn back.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/AJ%20Sacher.jpg)*AJ Sacher* Like Game 1, AJ played [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) naming [Breakthrough](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Breakthrough), which missed, but revealed [Firestorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Firestorm) and some dredgers. The following turn dredge revealed multiple dredgers, but Ari was still forced to pass the turn back without another play, all the while attempting to guess what hate he had coming his way.


“[Yixlid Jailer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yixlid+Jailer)?”  

“Yup,” offered AJ with a shrug. “Go.”  

“So obvious. Right after I used my [Firestorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Firestorm)s to keep going.”


Over the next few turns, [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial) kicked out a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) and a [Viridian Zealot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viridian+Zealot) to start attacking, while Ari only had an anemic-looking Narcomeba holding back the Jailer.


“Ugh,” said Ari, “I have no clue what I'm doing in this format.”


When AJ brought out [Magus of the Moon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Magus+of+the+Moon) to go with Yxilid Jailer, Ari saw no more outs without his two [Firestorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Firestorm)s and scooped up his cards.


“Yeah, that was pretty much just him failing to get there,” offered AJ after the match.


AJ Sacher defeats Ari Lax 2-0


  


Saturday, 7:45 p.m. - Old Pros, Same Game
-----------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

When Grand Prixs feature old cards, old players come out in droves to play with their favorites. This includes a number of former pros, names you may or may not remember, from days when, for instance, no one was blogging about them and posting pictures for the entire world to see.


Ah, the good old days.


But we were able to catch up with a few of the old guard as they came to game in Chicago.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Scott%20Lewis.jpg)*Scott Lewis* Scott Lewis is an Iowan who was part of a “Justice League” long before a few certain judges grabbed the name. Scott was a regular on the early tour, often qualifying season after season by PTQ if necessary. He said his last pro tour was “In Chicago, though I'm not sure when,” (bets are it might have been Bob Maher's Chicago PT) and his last high-level event of any kind was the Madison Team Trios Grand Prix a few years back.


For Lewis, still an occasional FNMer and local player, it's the people who bring him out. Friends he hasn't seen for years were what drew him this year.


“It was the location that brought me too,” added Lewis. “I would have played anything.”


Even though he's long removed from his days on the Tour, Lewis never really quit.


“I've never thought of myself as not playing Magic,” said Lewis.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Eric%20Froehlich.jpg)*Eric Froehlich* Eric Froehlich, on the other hand, hasn't played Magic in the past three years despite enjoying a breakout season in 2002 and being a storied member of the old “Magic Colony” (think Beach House). His last Pro Tour was, like Lewis, a team event, this time at Pro Tour Charleston.


So why come back after so much time?


“[Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). I have cast it since I was 12,” he said of the ubiquitous blue instant.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Craig%20Wescoe.jpg)*Craig Wescoe*  Craig Wescoe is a pros pro, as his name came up repeatedly when other “modern” pros were asked. And even if they didn't know him, they knew who he was.


Wescoe has recently hopped back on the train, qualifying for Pro Tour Hawaii just last weekend by winning a PTQ in Indianapolis, the same place he played in his last Grand Prix. For Wescoe, he never really quit, he just sort of took a break.


“No one ever quits Magic,” he said. “There was a period of a few years dedicated to academics in there.”


He's excited for Hawaii, as well, as he rattled of the names of a few other old pros who have qualified recently, including Osyp Lebedowicz and Brian Kibler.


  


Round 7 Feature Match: Gerry Thompson vs. David Caplan
------------------------------------------------------


*by Bill Stark*

“Any chance you'd want to switch sides?” Gerry Thompson asked his Canadian opponent as they sat down for their feature match, clearly biased as to which side of the table he wanted to sit on.


“Sure,” the amiable Caplan responded, getting up to rotate. From the peanut gallery, Hall of Famer and former Pro Tour-Champion Bob Maher was aghast.


“Don't let him sit on the side he's most comfortable on!” The Wisconsite jokingly exclaimed.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/FM7_Thompson.jpg)*Could Gerry Thompson win a second Grand Prix title?* Thompson is a well respected American pro originally from Minnesota with a host of Grand Prix Top 8s on his resume. He finally managed to seal the deal in 2008 with a win at Grand Prix-Denver. David Caplan hasn't had as much success on the Pro Tour scene, but is a respected Vintage and Legacy player with Top 8s in the respective formats' World Championships. The old format pro opened aggressively with [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) followed by [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf).


Gerry T wasn't about to allow the ‘Goyf onto the board, using [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) to find himself a [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) and attempting to take advantage of the fact Caplan had used all his mana to play the *Future Sight* rare. Caplan seemed nonplussed, revealing a [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) of his own, sticking the [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), and ending the turn with two creatures and a land to Gerry's now empty board.


Thompson tried to rebuild with a [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) followed by a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), but David interfered using [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to counter Gerry's creature. When Caplan played a second Mongoose and continued on the warpath, Gerry soon found himself at just 8 life. He furiously spun his Top to find a solution, ending up with [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) on the board as a chump blocker.


“That's right!” Bob Maher, the Invitational winner depicted on the card, said from the peanut gallery.


“Yeah, a lot of good you're doing me!” Gerry responded.


Caplan smiled at the two players' antics, but spent most of his turn figuring out the best method of killing his opponent. He played [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), giving him a count of five cards in his graveyard, then bashed in with his team, sending Gerry to 2. A post-combat [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) from David got a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) from Gerry, dropping the Midwest all-star to just 1, but Caplan had a [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) to force his third ‘Goose onto the board and send the match to a second game.


David Caplan 1, Gerry Thompson 0


[Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) was first on the board, entering play on the very first turn for Gerry Thompson. His opponent fired right back with [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) while Gerry made a second-turn [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant). Caplan's [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) targeting the 2/1 met a muffled cry of “No!” from spectator Bob Maher, but it wasn't enough to keep the *Ravnica* rare from going to the graveyard straight off the stack. It looked like Thompson had few in any counters in hand.


Caplan decided to test that theory, dropping [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) then playing [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). The beatstick hit the table unmolested, and threatened to quickly send the match to Caplan in similar fashion to the first if Thompson didn't come up with some defense. Trying to do exactly that, Gerry played [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize), nabbing a [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) from David's hand, then played a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) of his own.


A flurry of [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)s was the next series of plays, with David Caplan using not one, not two, but *three* copies of the card to strand his opponent on just one land, an [Underground Sea](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Underground+Sea).
