Still, with [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) going and a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) holding down the fort, Gerry looked to be in good shape but David had a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to counter the Top after Gerry was forced to cash it in early and attempt to replay it.


The two players fell into a pattern of draw-go, both on just two lands. Gerry attempted [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant), but it was countered by [Spell Snare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Snare). A second copy of the card from Thompson was met with Fire of Fire/Ice fame, but Thompson had [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to run cover and his 2/1 started putting him ahead in the card count. He even found a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) of his own to give David a taste of his own land destruction medicine, leaving Caplan on just two lands.


Gerry Thompson had seen a string of solid hits from a combination of [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) and his draw step, each time revealing a land to Bob and taking zero damage. Caplan appeared to be getting a bit disgruntled with his opponent's good luck, but Thompson kept right on at it, revealing an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) to skip damage yet again. He added [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) to his board of the Confidant and [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), and when Caplan played [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose), Gerry hit blindly off [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance), revealing [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) for the free counter.


A few turns later, Gerry managed to land [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) to complete his lock, and David looked all but out. When Gerry was able to present a relevant clock shortly after, Caplan packed it in for a third game.


David Caplan 1, Gerry Thompson 1


The two players started off with their favorite plays of the match so far, Gerry on [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) and David on [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose). The first two-drop on the board was [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) for Gerry Thompson, but when Caplan tried for a two-drop to call his own in [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), Thompson fired right back with [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), countering the creature. A second Caplan [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) resolved successfully.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/FM7_Caplan.jpg)*David Caplan, a master of “old” formats* Of course, David's [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) wasn't long for the world. [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) got rid of the creature for Gerry, and he followed up with [Diabolic Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diabolic+Edict) to Nail David's [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose). The life totals stood 19-15 in David's favor, who used [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) to kill Gerry's [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant). With [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) going, and facing an opponent low on mana, Gerry tried to take advantage of the situation by playing a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). Caplan had no counter for the critter, and it started munching on his life total, dropping him all the way to 15.


Still, the wily Canuck wasn't out of tricks. Gerry activated his Top to look at the top three cards of his deck, then responded with a sac land activation. That would allow him to search out a land, then look at the top three cards after doing so, seeing a fresh set for the following turn. David responded with [Submerge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Submerge) targeting his opponent's [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf), putting the critter back on top of Gerry's deck. Thompson tried to cash in his Top to draw the beater, but David was ready for that with a [Stifle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stifle), and Gerry lost his attacker to the convoluted series of plays.


Thompson continued trying to draw down David's resources with his Top. David spent a good portion of his cards dealing with back-to-back [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)s from Gerry, and it left him with little more than lands. Gerry, meanwhile, had two cards in hand, a sac land, and an active Divining Top. It didn't look good for David Caplan, but he wasn't going down without a fight. A topdecked [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) yielded some goods, and he managed to stick a fully-powered [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose).


The 3/3 immediately went on the aggro, dropping Gerry to 10 over the course of a few turns and Thompson found himself again on the backfoot. He used [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) to find [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant), which he attempted to play. David used his final two cards to [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), and Gerry furiously used Top to find help, cashing one in and playing a second. The Mongoose munched him to 4 life, two attacks away from a victory for Caplan.


[Sower of Temptation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sower+of+Temptation) hit the board for Gerry, but would be little more than a chump blocker against his opponent's Mongoose. David plucked a juicy [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) from the top of his deck, down to a single card in hand, and quickly played it. He then attacked, and Gerry took the damage rather than waste his 2/2 blocking; he fell to just 1 life. Was it possible Gerry was going to lose this game after seeming to be so far ahead for so long?


The [Sower of Temptation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sower+of+Temptation) was moved to the red zone to chump block, and David flipped the card he had drawn for the turn: [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt). Gerry checked his life total, looked at the [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) in his hand, and nodded in defeat.


“You're kidding me! You didn't draw *anything* from that Top?” David asked, shocked.


David Caplan 2, Gerry Thompson 1


  


Saturday, 8:38 p.m. – Owen Turtenwald Saves the Day
---------------------------------------------------


*by Bill Stark*

Let's pretend for a moment that it's Round 3 of the largest North American Grand Prix in history. You sit down to play your match, pile shuffle your deck and, horror of horrors, realize there are 11 cards missing from your it! In a panic, you recall that during your Round 2 match, you forgot to pick up your graveyard after the match and are now missing those cards. What do you do?


If you're Illinois native Noah Swartz, you accept a game loss for your error, then frantically rush around the tournament hall to see if you can find 11 replacements for the missing cards! That's exactly what happened, but as Noah moved from the Lost and Found to each dealer in turn, it began to dawn on him that he probably wouldn't be able to find the replacements in time. Enter Owen Turtenwald.


Busy enjoying his third of three byes, Owen, who made the finals of the last Legacy Grand Prix in Columbus, was surprised when a winded Swartz rushed up to him. “Owen, give me your deck!” The young player huffed, while Owen looked on with a raised eyebrow. It turns out Owen and Noah were playing the exact same seventy five cards, making Owen's deck a perfect replacement for Noah's for one round. Turtenwald shipped the deck, then went off to hunt down additional copies of cards for his friends. That gave Swartz just enough time to come back from the 0-1 hole he dug himself and win the match.


Owen Turtenwald; unassuming hero (at least for Noah Swartz) of Grand Prix-Chicago!


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/OwenSwartz.jpg)*Owen Turtenwald (L) saved the day for his friend Noah Swartz.*


  


Round 8 Feature Match: Gavin Verhey vs. Michael Jacob
-----------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

Michael Jacob is the reigning U.S. Champion and World's Team Champion (alongside luminaries Paul Cheon and Sam Black). Gavin Verhey is a longtime junior-level competitor who broke through at Pro Tour Berlin. The winner was guaranteed to make day two, as both players stood at 6-1 after seven long rounds, making their pairing at the feature match table fairly predictable.


Said Verhey, “I said down and I said to Micheal ‘I'm waiting for the feature match announcement.' And there it was.”


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Gavin-Verhey.jpg)*Gavin Verhey.* Despite their success, neither player was particularly enthused about the format.


“All the decks in legacy suck,” said Michael.  

“It's true,” quipped Verhey.  

“All my extended decks could beat all these legacy decks.”  

“It's true, I built a faeries deck that was almost Extended Faeries.”


**Game 1**  

Michael won the roll, kept, and led with [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial) off a [Taiga](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Taiga), while Gavin played [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains), go.


A [Survival of the Fittest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Survival+of+the+Fittest) was [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)ed on Michael's second turn, while Gavin merely played [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory), go.


The second Survival from Jacob resolved, and was immediately used to pitch [Squee, Goblin Nabob](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squee%2C+Goblin+Nabob), fetching out [Mesmeric Fiend](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mesmeric+Fiend).


Gavin cycled [Eternal Dragon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eternal+Dragon) in Michael's end step, and Michael [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Aether%2BVial)ed in the [Mesmeric Fiend](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mesmeric+Fiend) on Gavin's turn, taking [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares). Gavin revealed a hand full of lands, [Wrath of God](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wrath+of+God), and [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will).


On his upkeep, [Squee, Goblin Nabob](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squee%252C%2BGoblin%2BNabob) jumped back into Michael's hand, then jumped right back out to find [Genesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Genesis) before a [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) on [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) continued to strip Gavin's dwindling hand.


With little else to do, Gavin swung with his [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory) into an [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial) with two counters and Survival mana up. Michael responded by Survivaling for [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) and [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Aether%2BVial)ing it in. Gavin's draw step had yielded a [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares), allowing the Factory to get through un-'Goyfed.


Michael again spent his upkeep using Survival, searching up [Anger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Anger) and [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf). The Flashback on [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) removed Gavin's [Wrath of God](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wrath+of+God), clearing the way for [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) and the Fiend to attack for six, sending Gavin to 12.


When his next draw step yielded nothing, Gavin simply opted to move on to Game 2.


**Game 2**  

With no mulligans, Jacob made the first play of the game with a turn two [Mesmeric Fiend](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mesmeric+Fiend). [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) hid some cards in response, and the fiend took [Enlightened Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Enlightened+Tutor), leaving two [Moat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moat)s in Gavin's hand, among other things.


What Gavin hid was revealed the next turn as he played [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) and [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) before passing the turn back. The Top, however, wasn't long for the world as Michael had [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip), a popular sideboard card this weekend.


Gavin's next play was an [Aura of Silence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aura+of+Silence), hoping to slow down the Survival engine. Jacob simply swung with the Fiend and played [Eternal Witness](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eternal+Witness), returning [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip). Gavin played draw go, missing important land drop number four to power out his [Moat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moat)s. Jacob swung Gavin to 14 before a [Harmonic Sliver](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harmonic+Sliver) destroyed the [Aura of Silence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aura+of+Silence).


Shrugging, Gavin simply ran out [Moat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moat) #1 after hitting land #4, aware of the [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip) in Michaels, um, grip. However, Jacob, sensing a window of opportunity, chose instead to resolve [Survival of the Fittest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Survival+of+the+Fittest), activating it immediately to search up a [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise). Naturally, [Squee, Goblin Nabob](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squee%2C+Goblin+Nabob) was the creature discarded.


Gavin wasn't out yet, as an [Engineered Explosives](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Engineered+Explosives) destroyed Survival and released his [Enlightened Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Enlightened+Tutor) from the [Mesmeric Fiend](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mesmeric+Fiend). But Michael simply replaced the lost discard with a [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress), revealing [Humility](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Humility), two [Counterspell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterspell), [Moat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moat), and [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares). In order to save everyone the rules headaches, he took the [Humility](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Humility).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/Michael-Jacob.jpg)*Michael Jacob.* “I suspected you had that,” offered Michael before playing a second [Survival of the Fittest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Survival+of+the+Fittest).


Gavin showed that he too could search his library for silver bullets, with an upkeep [Enlightened Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Enlightened+Tutor) fetching [Crucible of Worlds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crucible+of+Worlds), which allowed him to start recurring [Flooded Strand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flooded+Strand).


However, Michael fired back by searching up both [Mesmeric Fiend](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mesmeric+Fiend) and [Magus of the Moon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Magus+of+the+Moon), while Gavin had only one land available and couldn't counter. Fiend predictably took [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares), clearing the way for [Magus of the Moon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Magus+of+the+Moon). The Magus left Gavin with only an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) and a [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains) for non-red mana.


The [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip) from the start of the game then made a return appearance and destroyed [Moat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Moat). Michael attacked for three and passed the turn.


Another [Enlightened Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Enlightened+Tutor) found [Circle of Protection: Green](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Circle+of+Protection%3A+Green), which, red mana or not, could severely hamper Jacob's offense...if he didn't have [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip). He did, and he played it during his upkeep before passing priority, earning a trip to day two.


Michael Jacob defeats Gavin Verhey 2-0


  


Round 9 Feature Match: Mark Herberholz vs. Nick Wise
----------------------------------------------------


*by Bill Stark*

Nick Wise is no stranger to the feature match area, receiving not one but two such matches at Grand Prix-Kansas City. That said, it was his opponent Mark Herberholz hogging the spotlight from the peanut gallery as they sat down to battle in the final round of Swiss play. Mark, or Heezy as he's known to his friends, is a former Pro Tour champion emerging victorious in Honolulu just a few seasons ago. That format was Standard, but the players were awash in a world of Legacy for Grand Prix-Chicago.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/FM10_Wise.jpg)*Rookie Nick Wise takes on the veteran pro for Day 2.* The two settled in to the first game, the match an elimination bout as they had both entered the round at 6-1-1. All 6-2s would be making Day 2, so their draw was a functional loss and either needed a win to proceed to Sunday action. Wise got things started with a [Mother of Runes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mother+of+Runes) and [Figure of Destiny](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Figure+of+Destiny) off of [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains) and [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland). Herberholz led with standard [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)/Top lands in the form of [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta) and [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island).


The Figure was soon on the rampage as a 2/2, joined on the table by [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte). Mark did his best to stay in the game playing [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) but could only watch silently as the [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Umezawa%25E2%2580%2599s%2BJitte) was equipped to Figure and the two combined dropped his life to 9. With Mother of the Runes active, Mark would need two removal spells simultaneously to deal with both creatures. He played [Thirst for Knowledge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thirst+for+Knowledge), carefully examining the top three cards of his deck. Not happy with what he saw, he conceded to a somewhat surprised Nick Wise.


Nick Wise 1, Mark Herberholz 0


Mark kicked the second game off with a one-drop in the form of [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top), but Nick also had a one-drop in the form of [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress). The discard spell, representing a color not seen from Wise's deck in the first game, stole a [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) from Heezy and prevented the Pro Tour champ from establishing his deck's combo lock on the second turn. Wise followed up his first [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress) with a second, but it was countered by Mark's [Spellstutter Sprite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellstutter+Sprite). That opened the doors for Nick to land [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial), which would provide him access to free creatures down the road, protected from Mark's counterspells.


It was Herberholz, however, who was on the war path using [Spellstutter Sprite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellstutter+Sprite) to start getting aggressive against Wise. Mark cashed in his Top for the top card of his deck, then discarded it to a [Thirst for Knowledge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thirst+for+Knowledge). Nick capitalized by Extirpating the pesky artifact, shutting Mark out of hitting it for the rest of the game.


That left Herberholz with little choice but to stay on the offensive, and he did exactly that playing [Venser, Shaper Savant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Venser%2C+Shaper+Savant) to bounce his opponent's [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial). Nick responded by putting a free [Figure of Destiny](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Figure+of+Destiny) into play, then continued taking damage from the flying [Spellstutter Sprite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellstutter+Sprite). The game was looking bad for him as Mark was way out ahead on land and had managed to find an [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte) to suit up his [Spellstutter Sprite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellstutter+Sprite). Equipping the artifact to the 1/1 flyer meant Wise's [Mother of Runes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mother+of+Runes) was soon dead to a -1/-1 activation.


Trying to stay in it, Nick played [Jotun Grunt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jotun+Grunt), and even managed to connect during an attack, leaving the totals at 16-12 in Herberholz' favor. Mark fired right back with a [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique), but found his [Spellstutter Sprite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellstutter+Sprite) dead to a Nick Wise [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares). He didn't seem to care, equipping his [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Umezawa%2527s%2BJitte) to [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) and bashing Nick to 5. Nick got right back in to the red zone himself, putting Mark at 4, but the young Nebraska player was facing a lethal counter attack. When Mark didn't forget to turn his flyer sideways, Nick conceded.


Nick Wise 1, Mark Herberholz 1


A first-turn [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial) from Nick Wise was met with [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) from Mark Herberholz, who removed a [Daze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daze) from the game to pay the alternative casting cost of the card. Wise shrugged nonchalantly, then played a [Figure of Destiny](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Figure+of+Destiny) on his second turn. Mark had [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) for his play, passing back to Wise with only a single blue mana open.


[Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) came down for Nick, the *Ravnica* rare a popular feature match denizen on the weekend. That merited a spin of the Top for Herberholz, but he didn't find what he was looking for and the 2/1 resolved successfully. Instead of a counter, however, Mark revealed he *did* have an answer to the sneaky Wizard using [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) on his turn to answer the Invitational card before it gave Wise any free draws. Mark then got on the board with a creature of his own, playing [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique). The play didn't come with out cost, as Nick used a window to [Extirpate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Extirpate) Mark's [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)s, nabbing one of the counters from Herberholz' hand in the process.


The next plays centered around two casting cost spells with Nick resolving an [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte) while Heezy cashed in his Divining Top to play [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance). Once he re-played his artifact the following turn, he was going to have his lock established and the world would be looking up for him. Of course, considering the fact Nick Wise was still stuck on two lands well in to the mid game while Mark had more lands *and* more cards in hand, it was already looking pretty bad for the youngster.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpchi09/FM10_Heezy.jpg)*Mark Herberholz looks to squeeze in to Day 2.*Heezy used his own copy of [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte) to legend rule Nick's, then spun his Top with a sac land to [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) an attempted [Tidehollow Sculler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tidehollow+Sculler) from Wise. Turn after turn Nick tried to maneuver a spell onto the board, and each time Mark was able to spin his Top into the right converted mana cost to stymie all those efforts. Sensing the coast was clear, Mark dropped a [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) to join his [Mutavault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mutavault) in the red zone. Wise fell to 20 after gaining life from [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Umezawa%25E2%2580%2599s%2BJitte) and a [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares).


The 5-point clock Herberholz had put together with [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) and [Mutavault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mutavault) became a 3-point clock as Nick used [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) to kill his opponent's creature-land. Unfortunately for Nick, a second copy of the *Morningtide* standout was waiting for his opponent, and he was soon at 10 life. When his draws continued yielding no action he could finagle through Mark's [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)/Top combo, the Nebraska player fell to the Faerie and creature-land in defeat.


Mark Herberholz 2, Nick Wise 1
